# slate v2 10h auto proof transport selection

Objective:
Automate Slate v2 10h proof transport and selection closure; done when floor
elapses, packets close, and gates pass.

Goal plan:
docs/plans/2026-06-13-slate-v2-10h-auto-proof-transport-selection.md

Template:
docs/plans/templates/slate-auto.md

Primary template:
docs/plans/templates/slate-auto.md

Applied packs:
- none

Automation source:
- type: user-invoked `slate-auto`
- prompt / link: `[$slate-auto](/Users/zbeyens/git/plate-2/.agents/skills/slate-auto/SKILL.md) 10h`
- surface / route / package: current Slate v2 private-alpha tree in `.tmp/slate-v2`, focused on proof transport, selection oracle hardening, stable editor behavior, and huge-document non-pagination correctness/perf
- invocation mode: timed mode
- minimum runtime / deadline: at least 10h active automation from 2026-06-14 00:31 CEST; target floor 2026-06-14 10:31 CEST
- completion threshold summary: run until the 10h minimum elapses, keep/revert/quarantine every active packet, avoid pagination unless explicitly requested, and close the plan with proof gates plus final `check-complete`

First checkpoint:
- Before implementation or broad exploration, copy every explicit prompt
  requirement into this plan as checkable rows: scope, non-goals, timing,
  stop conditions, deliverables, final handoff sections, verification surfaces,
  and success criteria.
- The initial checkpoint list is only the seed. After every loop, the
  supervisor must reconcile this plan against new evidence and may add, update,
  split, merge, retire, remove, reprioritize, or reopen checkpoints.
- Do not continue into implementation until first extraction is complete or
  explicitly marked N/A with reason.

Completion threshold:
- The run may hand off only after the 10h minimum active runtime has elapsed
  and the active packet has a keep/revert/quarantine decision.
- Before then, keep adding/running checkpoints from current evidence: proof
  transport gaps, selection oracle gaps, stable example browser proof, huge-doc
  non-pagination correctness/perf, benchmark honesty, `slate-browser` helper
  promotion, API/docs mismatch, research leads, and workflow slowdowns.
- Immediate P0s: start from the previous 8h closure, keep pagination deferred
  by default, target `slate-browser` click-offset transport, then harden
  selection oracles before perf.
- Closure is legal only when required behavior, visual/native selection,
  package/API, mobile/raw-device claim-width, huge-document, docs/skill repair,
  changed-list, review-attention, stopping-checkpoint, workflow-slowdown, and
  final handoff rows are complete, explicitly deferred, or N/A with evidence,
  and `node .agents/skills/autogoal/scripts/check-complete.mjs docs/plans/2026-06-13-slate-v2-10h-auto-proof-transport-selection.md`
  passes.

Verification surface:
- Previous evidence anchor: `docs/plans/2026-06-13-slate-v2-8h-automation.md`
  P93/P95 green gates and P96 final completion.
- `.tmp/slate-v2` source/test ownership for `slate-browser/playwright`,
  `playwright/integration/examples/**`, `packages/slate-react/**`, and
  huge-document/stable example routes.
- Focused `slate-browser` package build/typecheck/unit tests when helpers
  change.
- Focused Playwright rows for editable-voids, richtext, plaintext,
  synced-blocks, huge-document, markdown shortcuts, placeholder, and hidden DOM
  when evidence names them.
- Screenshot/geometry/native-selection proof when a browser-visible issue or
  double-highlight/caret-path risk is found.
- Huge-document benchmark metrics only after behavior proof is green, and only
  for non-pagination lanes unless the user explicitly requests pagination.
- Parent `pnpm install` plus source/mirror audit when `.agents/rules/**`
  changes.
- `bun check`, `bun check:full` when browser-facing/runtime proof changed, and
  final `check-complete.mjs` after all rows close.

Constraints:
- Slate v2 private alpha by default: no release, publish, changeset, PR, or
  branch readiness unless the prompt explicitly asks.
- Run Slate v2 behavior commands from `.tmp/slate-v2`; parent repo commands
  prove plans, docs, skills, and templates only.
- Behavior proof beats perf. Native/visual proof beats model-only selection.
- No hidden debounce or fake stress fixture wins.
- Pagination is explicit opt-in only. Do not infer pagination from
  virtualization, huge-document, perf debt, skip ledgers, supervision mode, or
  generic architecture backlog. Queue pagination as deferred with owner
  `slate-plan` unless the user explicitly requests it.
- Do not patch Plate when the run is scoped to Slate v2.

Boundaries:
- Source of truth: live runtime `.tmp/slate-v2`; control docs under parent
  `docs/slate-v2/**`, `docs/research/**`, active plan, and source rules.
- Allowed edit scope: Slate v2 runtime/tests/benchmarks/docs/research/skills
  when owned by evidence; keep speculative runtime packets reversible.
- Browser surfaces: local examples and route Playwright rows for selection,
  editable voids, richtext/plaintext, hidden DOM, markdown shortcuts,
  synced-blocks, and huge-document staged/virtualized/auto non-pagination.
- Package/API surfaces: `slate-browser` proof helpers first; `slate-react` or
  other runtime packages only when proof points there.
- Agent/skill surfaces: patch source `.agents/rules/**` only for repeated
  workflow misses; never hand-edit generated `SKILL.md`.
- Docs/research surfaces: update research artifacts only when research leads
  are used/promoted; write compact evidence, not raw dumps.
- Non-goals: no release/publish/changeset/PR readiness; no raw mobile claims
  without real device lane; no pagination unless explicitly requested; no broad
  external issue ledgers until local proof transport/oracles are stronger.

Output budget strategy:
- Use exact owner files, focused `rg -l` / counts, and short `sed` ranges
  before broad scans.
- Write broad skip audits or research scans to `.tmp/**` or docs artifacts and
  inspect summaries/slices.
- Exclude generated site output, raw issue JSON, logs, binaries, `node_modules`,
  `.next`, `.turbo`, and benchmark artifacts unless named.
- Managed Playwright commands must be serialized; file reads and package-local
  non-server tests may run in parallel.

Blocked condition:
- Hard block only if all safe owners are exhausted and the remaining move needs
  commit/PR/destructive authority, unavailable raw-device hardware, missing
  credentials/tooling, explicit pagination work, or a user-only product/API
  decision not covered by `vision`.
- Do not block while a safe alternate checkpoint remains runnable. In timed or
  batch mode, queue soft questions for final handoff.
- Do not hand off before a timed minimum runtime has elapsed because the obvious
  backlog looks empty. Enter supervision mode and infer the next checkpoint from
  `vision`, current evidence, weak proofs, benchmark gaps, API/docs
  mismatch, issue/test harvest gaps, and workflow slowdowns.

Mutation rules:
- Add a checkpoint when a new failure, missing oracle, missing metric, API smell,
  visual proof gap, workflow slowdown, taste gap, or owner gap appears.
- Update a checkpoint when evidence changes its scope, priority, owner, command,
  exit rule, or proof surface.
- Split a checkpoint when it hides multiple owners or one prompt would become
  too large.
- Merge checkpoints when overlap confuses routing or two rows always close
  together.
- Retire or remove checkpoints that are stale, superseded, irrelevant,
  duplicated, or contradicted by current evidence. Record the reason in the
  mutation ledger.
- Reopen a closed checkpoint when new evidence invalidates its proof.
- Reprioritize after every loop. The next checkpoint is chosen from current
  evidence, not from the original row order.
- The supervisor is not stuck on this template or the initial prompt plan. The
  user's latest request, `vision`, and current source evidence outrank
  stale plan rows.

|------|---------|----------|

| `slate-auto` source rule read | yes | `.agents/skills/slate-auto/SKILL.md` read completely; pagination opt-in rule confirmed. |
| `vision` read as checkpoint zero | yes | `.agents/skills/vision/SKILL.md` read; behavior/visual proof and no fake mobile/debounce rules applied. |

| Dynamic checkpoint policy accepted | yes | Checkpoint supervisor table includes add/update rows and mutation ledger loop 0. |

Work Checklist:
- [x] First checkpoint complete: every explicit prompt requirement, scope
      boundary, timing constraint, stop condition, deliverable, final handoff
      section, verification surface, and success criterion is copied into this
      plan as checkable checkpoints before implementation.
- [x] Short objective, completion threshold, verification surface, constraints,
      boundaries, and blocked condition are concrete.
- [x] Invocation mode, minimum runtime/deadline, stop-question policy, remaining
      backlog ladder, and supervision-mode fallback are recorded.
- [x] Checkpoint supervisor table has been reconciled at least once after the
      initial seed.
- [x] Each loop ends with a checkpoint mutation decision: add, update, split,
      merge, retire, remove, reopen, reprioritize, or no-change with reason.
- [x] Current-tree/status packet recorded before new runtime patches.
      Evidence: prior P96 closure, roadmap, owner files, and clickTextOffset
      implementation read before P1 skip-width edit.
- [x] Behavior proof packet recorded for every in-scope stable editor family or
      explicitly skipped/deferred with reason.
- [x] Visual/native selection proof packet recorded for browser-visible
      selection/editing risks or explicitly scoped.
- [x] Missing oracle packets are written, kept, reverted, quarantined, or
      deferred with owner and proof command.
- [x] Repeated browser proof patterns are promoted to `slate-browser` or queued
      with reason.
- [x] Mobile/raw-device proof is run or the claim width is explicitly limited;
      Playwright viewport proof is not recorded as raw-device proof.
- [x] Huge-document correctness smoke is run or deferred with owner and reason.
- [x] Perf packet runs only after correctness is green, or is marked N/A for
      this run.
- [x] Package/API hard cuts, aliases, exports, and docs/API consistency are
      audited when in scope.
- [x] Docs/north-star/rule consolidation is applied when a reusable decision is
      accepted, or marked N/A.
- [x] Workflow slowdowns are logged and avoidable repeats are repaired in the
      owner skill/script/gate.
- [x] Packet ledger contains one row per proof, bug fix, oracle, benchmark,
      docs, or skill packet.
- [x] Changed list is current and includes only this run.
- [x] Needs-your-attention list is ranked and capped at five items.
- [x] Stopping checkpoints are queued or marked none.
- [x] Autoreview/review gate is run for non-trivial implementation diffs or
      marked N/A with reason.
- [x] Agent-native review is run for `.agents/**`, commands, skills, hooks, or
      prompt/tooling changes, or marked N/A with reason.
- [x] Output budget discipline is followed: broad scans are capped or written
      to artifacts instead of streamed.

Findings:
- P1: `clickTextOffset` itself did not need a helper/API change for the known
  child-root arrow and richtext mark-click blockers. The editable-void row was
  stale Chromium-only proof; it now passes on Chromium, Firefox, and WebKit with
  mobile explicitly skipped as viewport/raw-device scoped.
- P2: The richtext multi-leaf replacement test title claimed mouse drag while
  using `selectDOM`; that was a bad oracle. It now uses native cross-leaf drag
  via `dragTextRange`, and `slate-browser` can express the whole selection
  contract as one replayable scenario assertion.
- P3: Stable editor families are green after P2. No runtime regressions surfaced
  in editable voids, hidden DOM, markdown shortcuts, placeholder/custom
  placeholder, richtext history/selection, plaintext selection/navigation, or
  visual-native smoke.
- P4: Huge-doc staged/virtualized non-pagination behavior is green for the
  current smoke lanes. The previous ShiftDown/ShiftUp and select-all/delete
  pain points are covered by bounded rows and screenshot-visible no-double
  selection proof.
- P5: Current staged huge-doc keyboard metrics do not justify optimization
  before research: 5k staged lanes are around one frame for ShiftDown/ShiftUp
  paint and under 30ms p95 for select-all/delete/undo in the sampled benchmark.
- P6: Existing WPT research already had the best current proof lead for vertical
  caret movement. Rerunning it passed; fresh broad GitHub queries were not
  useful enough to clone or promote.
- P7: The proof-helper docs were behind the API. That is a real supervisor
  miss pattern because stale helper docs make future agents re-invent fragile
  browser proof instead of using the durable API.
- P8: Local Playwright `list` reporter plus body-only JSON attachments is not
  enough for overnight supervision. Durable proof needs a filesystem file that
  the next loop can inspect without opening the reporter UI.
- P9/P10: The visual selection lane is stronger now: it is not Chromium-only,
  and the richtext multi-leaf row no longer simulates the selected DOM range
  directly.
- P11: `Chromium reporter path` is a stale skip reason for at least one current
  stable behavior row. Treat the remaining uses as suspicious until proved.
- P12: The reporter-path pattern is cleaned up. The only failed widening was
  Firefox isolated inline-link native drag, where native selected text remains
  empty after repeated drag attempts; Chromium/WebKit cover that row.
- P14: Four inline editing rows were stale Chromium-only coverage. They pass on
  Firefox and WebKit without code changes.
- P15: Editable-void keyboard boundary/projection proof was also stale
  Chromium-only coverage. Firefox/WebKit pass the same assertions.
- P16: Richtext structured cut/paste payload proof was stale Chromium-only
  coverage. Firefox/WebKit pass the same assertions.
- P18: The Firefox inline-link failure was not a native-browser impossibility.
  Raw Firefox contenteditable selected the isolated link; the Slate route lost
  the expanded range after mouseup. The runtime fix is therefore scoped to
  Firefox mouseup collapse, not a broad selection rewrite.
- P20: The fast gate did its job. The Firefox detector needed a top-level regex;
  after that lint fix, the full fast tree and current-source browser row are
  green.
- P21: The exact repaired link path now has screenshot-backed proof. Firefox
  and WebKit show a single link highlight; no duplicate native/projected layer
  is visible.
- P22: The broader visual-native selection suite still passes after the new
  row, so the visual proof did not create a suite-local regression or fake green.
- P23: The current source tree is fast-gate clean after the visual row addition.
- P24: The modified inline-link behavior and visual rows do not use fake-green
  early returns. Browser scoping is explicit skip or real Firefox setup logic.
- P25: Full Firefox `inlines` stayed green after the route/runtime repair. The
  skipped rows are existing explicit triple-click browser-scope skips, not the
  repaired drag path.
- P26: Firefox richtext native selection/history stayed green after the shared
  mouseup replay repair.
- P27: Firefox plaintext selection/navigation stayed green after the shared
  mouseup replay repair.
- P28: External source research supports the current shape rather than
  challenging it. ProseMirror delays/fences selection synchronization during
  pointer gestures; Lexical stores/restores selection for targeted browser
  event-order quirks. WPT/upstream Slate did not provide a stronger direct
  oracle for this exact Firefox inline-link path.
- P29: Huge-document non-pagination critical selection/editing smoke remains
  green after the Firefox selection replay repair.
- P30: Huge-document bounded repeated vertical selection remains green and
  screenshot-clean on Firefox staged and virtualized lanes.
- P31: Fresh-build staged keyboard metrics remain stable. No perf patch is
  justified from this sample: ShiftDown/repeated ShiftDown stay around one
  frame and long tasks remain zero.
- P32: Full Firefox editable-voids stayed green, including same-runtime child
  root, native input selection, paste/drop, and selectionchange noise rows.
- P33: Firefox hidden-content and placeholder routes stayed green, including
  hidden/materialized selection matrix rows and placeholder selected-text/caret
  rows. Skips are explicit IME/WebKit-style scoped rows.
- P34: Firefox markdown shortcuts stayed green across typing, list/heading
  transforms, undo/redo, and caret-placement rows.
- P35: WebKit full `inlines` stayed green after the helper/test changes. The
  repaired inline-link drag row passed in the full suite.
- P36: Chromium full `inlines` stayed green too. The touched inline route now
  has full desktop-engine route proof.
- P37: Source scope matches the proof: no broad replay, no helper reuse, no
  non-Firefox path, no overwrite while an expanded native selection still
  exists.
- P38: Fast tree remains green after the current run's implementation and proof
  changes.
- P39: Drag oracle audit did not find another dirty `selectDOM` masquerading as
  native drag.
- P40: WebKit richtext/plaintext selection-sensitive slices are green. The
  richtext command matched five rows, so the proof is useful but intentionally
  not described as a full WebKit richtext route sweep.
- P41: Chromium richtext/plaintext selection-sensitive slices are green with
  the same shape as P40, so post-P18 desktop richtext/plaintext proof is now
  current across Chromium, Firefox, and WebKit for these focused rows.
- P42: WebKit non-inline stable routes are green after the selection/runtime
  work: editable voids, hidden-content blocks, markdown shortcuts, and
  placeholder passed 55 rows with 5 explicit scoped skips.
- P43: Chromium non-inline stable routes are green after the selection/runtime
  work: editable voids, hidden-content blocks, markdown shortcuts, and
  placeholder passed all 60 rows.
- P44: Fast tree remains green after the current browser-proof wave.

Decisions and tradeoffs:
- Keep P2: native drag helper promotion is better than another handwritten
  coordinate helper in `richtext.test.ts`; it strengthens generated scenarios
  and keeps future test repairs out of copy-paste proof soup.
- Keep P5 metrics as proof of current state, not a before/after optimization
  claim. No runtime perf packet was attempted because correctness and measured
  p95s are already stable for the sampled staged lanes.
- Keep P7 README docs as the durable owner for reusable `slate-browser`
  proof-helper usage; no `.agents/**` rule patch is needed because the miss was
  local API docs drift, not repeated skill topology failure.
- Keep P8 helper because it converts an agent workflow weakness into a reusable
  proof primitive. Do not patch pagination rows yet; pagination remains
  explicit opt-in.
- Keep P10 visual smoke upgrade because it removes another weak `selectDOM`
  setup from a user-visible selection proof row.
- Keep P18 because it deletes a false skip, strengthens `slate-browser` drag
  direction, and repairs the route-owned Firefox collapse without changing
  healthy Chromium/WebKit behavior.
- Keep P20 because the lint fix is behavior-equivalent, the fast tree is green,
  and the browser row was rerun after rebuilding current runtime source.
- Keep P21 because it turns the riskiest part of P18 into durable visual proof
  instead of trusting model/native text assertions alone.
- Keep P22 because it proves the whole selection-smoke file still works with
  the added inline-link row and current skip accounting.
- Keep P23 because it closes the lint/type/unit side of the visual spec change.
- Keep P24 because it validates the current proof shape without another code
  patch; the slowdown is command-shape, not runtime.
- Keep P25 because it proves the repaired Firefox mouseup path does not break
  the broader inline example workflow.
- Keep P26 because it covers the same shared root-interaction path on richtext
  native selection/history, not only inline links.
- Keep P27 because it covers the simplest native text-selection path, where a
  broad replay bug would show quickly.
- Keep P28 as a no-code research promotion. It prevents repeated wandering and
  says the current proof, not another runtime rewrite, is the right next state.
- Keep P29 because it refreshes the user's historically sensitive huge-doc
  selection/select-all lane without entering pagination.
- Keep P30 because it refreshes the historically painful ShiftDown/ShiftUp
  projected-selection lane and confirms no double-highlight visually.
- Keep P31 as benchmark state, not an optimization claim. It gives current
  before/latest metrics and says the next win is not a blind perf patch.
- Keep P32 because it covers the nested editable-root surface most likely to be
  hurt by a root interaction selection replay.
- Keep P33 because it covers hidden DOM and empty placeholder selection surfaces
  without broadening into raw mobile or IME claims.
- Keep P34 because it refreshes the stable shortcut/typing family from the
  original automation scope.
- Keep P35 because it balances the Firefox-focused repair work with full-route
  WebKit coverage on the touched inline route.
- Keep P36 because it closes full Chromium/Firefox/WebKit route confidence for
  `inlines`.
- Keep P37 because it converts the risky part of the runtime change into a
  reviewed invariant: captured evidence only, Firefox only, after collapse only.
- Keep P38 because it proves the current tree is still lint/type/unit clean.
- Keep P39 because it closes the specific supervisor miss that caused the
  original dirty test shape.
- Keep P40 because it expands WebKit stable selection proof beyond `inlines`
  without a risky runtime patch. Do not overclaim the richtext slice as a full
  route sweep because the grep matched five rows.
- Keep P41 because it refreshes the Chromium side of the same proof family
  after the selection/helper changes, without pretending the row count is a
  full-route sweep.
- Keep P42 because it refreshes WebKit behavior outside inline/richtext/
  plaintext: editable void child roots, hidden/materialized DOM selection,
  markdown transforms, and placeholder selection all stayed green.
- Keep P43 because it refreshes the same non-inline stable route family on
  Chromium with current source and no skips.
- Keep P44 because lint/type/unit stayed green after the stable browser route
  batches and plan/docs updates.
